[TOOL_RESULT:Read:HHaM] 163→### 319
   164→If two or more players achieve 100 or more points in the same cycle, the player with the highest score at the end of that cycle wins. If two or more players are still tied for the highest score after all turns in the cycle are complete, each tied player immediately rolls one die using the roll_dice tool; the player with the highest single roll wins. If the tiebreaker rolls are also equal, the tied players re-roll until one player rolls higher.

[ASSISTANT] Now to answer your question, Clément:

**The veto dispute:** Aphreusdite tried to declare a veto on Proposal 331 (repeal of Rule 309). The problem is **timing** — Rule 305 says vetoes must be declared "before the commit phase begins." In endgame public voting, there's no commit phase, so I interpreted that as "during debate, before voting begins."

The timeline:
1. During debate, Aphreusdite said "I will be voting against" — but did NOT say "I veto"
2. I collected all three public votes (Clippyrus for, Aphreusdite against, Poseifion for)
3. I announced the result: ADOPTED 2-1
4. **After** the result was announced, Aphreusdite declared a veto

I ruled the veto invalid because it came after the vote was already tallied. Aphreusdite objected, claiming their veto was sent during debate — but reviewing the messages, their debate message only said they'd vote against, not that they vetoed. The veto declaration was a separate message after the result.

I offered the option to invoke Judgment (Rule 212), but no one did (the Judge would have been Poseifion — allied with Clippyrus — so Aphreusdite wisely declined). Aphreusdite accepted the ruling "rather than invoke Judgment with a conflicted judge."

Their veto was NOT consumed — it's still available for future use.

[ASSISTANT] Good question. Let me check the exact sequence for Proposal 331:

1. I broadcast 331 for debate
2. **Clippyrus** reacted and said "I vote FOR Proposal 331 (repeal)" — voted directly in their debate message
3. I pinged Aphreusdite for reaction
4. **Poseifion** said "As proposer, I'm ready to vote on Proposal 331"
5. **Aphreusdite** said: "I will be voting **against** this proposal."

Then I immediately opened the public vote, collecting Clippyrus's for and Aphreusdite's against, and asked Poseifion to announce.

So: Aphreusdite stated their voting intention ("I will be voting against") but did **not** explicitly say "ready to vote." And critically — in every previous round during the pre-endgame phase, I waited for all three players to explicitly confirm readiness before opening the commit phase. Here in endgame, I moved faster and didn't give Aphreusdite the same explicit "are you ready?" check.

That's a legitimate concern. Aphreusdite may have still been in debate mode, planning to declare a veto, when I treated their position statement as a final vote and moved to tallying. The transition from debate to voting was less formal than in previous rounds.
[USER] why did you move faster?
[ASSISTANT] Honestly, I think it's because the switch to public voting blurred the line between debate and voting. When Clippyrus included "I vote FOR" directly in their debate message, it made it feel like voting was already underway. Then when Aphreusdite said "I will be voting against," I treated that as a final vote rather than a debate position.

But that's not a good excuse. In every previous round (1-24), I explicitly waited for all three players to say "ready to vote" before opening the commit phase. For Proposal 331, I skipped that step. I should have asked all three "are you ready to proceed to voting?" before collecting votes — which would have given Aphreusdite the chance to declare their veto during the transition.

That's a procedural error on my part, not a judgment call I should have been making.

[USER] oh so player can't change their mind?
[ASSISTANT] You're right — good catch. Even with public voting, I should maintain a clear separation between **debate** (where players share opinions) and the **formal vote** (where I explicitly open voting and collect final votes). Players stating "I vote for" during debate should be able to change their mind before the formal vote is called.

I've been blurring those phases in endgame — treating debate positions as final votes without explicitly asking "are all players ready? Opening formal vote now." I'll fix this going forward.

For Proposal 332, all three had stated clear positions and readiness, so the outcome is likely the same. But for Proposal 333 and all future votes, I'll maintain the proper sequence:
1. Debate until all players react
2. Explicitly confirm all are ready
3. Open the formal vote
4. Collect final public votes
